  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_23df2b6f-82c6-418a-be19-7e2584c098ac'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1484921581" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484921581" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1484921581?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1484921581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16366563475425054268"><b>“They don’t want to hear about darkness and death. They want children’s tales about love and rebirth and silver dragons.<br/>Don’t we all.”</b><br/><br/>If what you are after is an uplifting children’s tale about love and rebirth and dragons (of many colours) then you have come to the right place. Dragons of Spring Dawning concludes the Dragonlance Chronicles in a classic confrontation of good and evil, bravery and selfless sacrifice, and, naturally, love. Oh, and dragons, a minor detail that.<br/><br/>I will admit: <b>my memo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16366563475425054268" style="display:none"><b>“They don’t want to hear about darkness and death. They want children’s tales about love and rebirth and silver dragons.<br />Don’t we all.”</b><br /><br />If what you are after is an uplifting children’s tale about love and rebirth and dragons (of many colours) then you have come to the right place. Dragons of Spring Dawning concludes the Dragonlance Chronicles in a classic confrontation of good and evil, bravery and selfless sacrifice, and, naturally, love. Oh, and dragons, a minor detail that.<br /><br />I will admit: <b>my memories of this book are better than the book itself.*</b> It is in some places rushed, in others underdeveloped. The composition suffers as the authors experiment with different narration techniques and so inserted into the chapters you’ll find songs, poems, excerpts from chronicles or retellings - but instead of being invigorating, it befuddles. It feels like suddenly in class Z family movie everybody started speaking pure Shakespearean to add some gravitas to the whole thing, which, you’ll agree, is quite silly. <br /><br />The <b>plot moves from cheesy to staged to improbable. But still, darn it, a good fun</b>. Whereas all the companions are accounted for in their neat arcs, Berem the Everyman finally takes the stage and proves to be the central puzzle piece. There are <b>some “aha!” moments when things fall into place, interspersed with “oh, well…” and “oh, no!” exclamations</b>, but I will brave a bet that irrespective of your sympathies and regardless which character was your favourite, <b>you should be satisfied with the ending</b>.<br /><br />I was, though each time my primary loyalty switched from protagonist to protagonist; from Tanis and Laurana when I was reading the Chronicles for the first time, to Kender to Raistlin (quite surprisingly, I have to say, but mayhaps I was over-sugared and needed something else). <br /><br />At the same time, <b>in spite of my initial awe, Dragonlance Chronicles never prompted me to read more of the Dragonlance world. It was a superb gateway for the inexperienced fantasy reader that I was, but for me even then it lacked the depth that would keep me ensnared for longer</b>. I moved on quickly and looking back from today’s perspective of a jaded fantasy pro, I am not surprised. I retain my fondness though. And I’d encourage you to give the Drangonlance Chronicles a try. <br /><br /><b>*Disclaimer: My rating is purely sentimental. Dragons of Spring Dawning is a read down the memory lane. If I were to rate it on the basis of my current standards and preferences, it would score 3 stars the most.</b><br /><br />Also in the series: <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484918749?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Autumn Twilight</a> <br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484921354" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Winter Night</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16366563475425054268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_906612705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/906612705" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/906612705?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=dungeons-and-dragons">dungeons-and-dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=dragonlance">dragonlance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer906612705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3603488725347352319"><i>Dragonqueen she was called in elven; Nilat the Corrupter, to the barbarians of the Plains; Tamex, the False Metal, so she was known in Thorbardin among the dwarves; Mai-tat, She of Many Faces was how they told of her in legends among the sea-faring people of Ergoth. Queen of Many Colors and of None, the Knights of Solamnia called her; defeated by Huma, banished from the land, long ago.<br/>Takhisis, Queen of Darkness, had returned.</i><br/><br/>A disastrous defeat has all but destroyed the free nations of Krynn, a</span>
  <span id="freeText3603488725347352319" style="display:none"><i>Dragonqueen she was called in elven; Nilat the Corrupter, to the barbarians of the Plains; Tamex, the False Metal, so she was known in Thorbardin among the dwarves; Mai-tat, She of Many Faces was how they told of her in legends among the sea-faring people of Ergoth. Queen of Many Colors and of None, the Knights of Solamnia called her; defeated by Huma, banished from the land, long ago.<br />Takhisis, Queen of Darkness, had returned.</i><br /><br />A disastrous defeat has all but destroyed the free nations of Krynn, and all hope appears to be lost. And now the dragonarmies are amassing at the ghastly Temple of Neraka, preparing to subjugate the whole world to the domination of the Dark Queen. But in a final act of defiance, a small band of heroes travel in secret to this stronghold of evil to rescue a lost friend, and to strike back one last time...<br /><br /><i>Dragons of Spring Dawning</i> saved the series. The second book (and honestly, much of this one) proved to be a huge disappointment, but in the end it deserves most of the love it gets. As usual, quality is low, entertainment value is high. The characters are shallow, the setting is amazing. And unlike the one in <i>Winter Night</i>, the storyline here really picks up again, almost going back to the level of <i>Autumn Twilight</i>.<br /><br />One group of characters that were particularly good in this final book were the villains. The villains in the first two books were perhaps even more one-dimensional than the protagonists, but that appears to have changed here. The only villain getting a considerable amount of spotlight is the Dragon Highlord known as the Dark Lady (who has become one of my favourite characters in this series), but the others are probably even better. Ariakas, the self-proclaimed Emperor of Ansalon, the death knight Lord Soth, and Takhisis herself are all memorable.<br /><br />In the end, I am glad I chose to give this series a try after nearly putting it aside because of all the negative reviews. It has <i>tons</i> of flaws, but there is a reason why it’s one of the most popular and influential fantasy series ever written.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3603488725347352319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

These books are fast paced, epic stories peopled with tons of great fantasy characters (elves, dwarves, knights, gnomes, dragons, magicians and sorcerers and even a minotaur sailor).         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2221201659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6323850202867966959">I've read this so many times now, but my youngest is eight and I wanted to read it to her, and her thirteen year old siblings were down for listening to the series again, so I thrilled in the chance to read it all aloud once again. It took a while to finish the Chronicles this time, but we got there right at the death of 2017. <br/><br/>I am so glad we did. <br/><br/><i>Spring Dawning</i> is nowhere near the best of the series (and I include the Chronicles in that assessment), but it does have have three things going for </span>
  <span id="freeText6323850202867966959" style="display:none">I've read this so many times now, but my youngest is eight and I wanted to read it to her, and her thirteen year old siblings were down for listening to the series again, so I thrilled in the chance to read it all aloud once again. It took a while to finish the Chronicles this time, but we got there right at the death of 2017. <br /><br />I am so glad we did. <br /><br /><i>Spring Dawning</i> is nowhere near the best of the series (and I include the Chronicles in that assessment), but it does have have three things going for it: plenty of Fizban, definitive Raistlin, and all the evidence we’ll ever need to prove Tanis is a massive dickhead.<br /><br />I've gone into details on these things elsewhere, but it is worth pointing out again that Tanis is one of the most despicable protagonists ever to be loved by folks in any IP with any modicum of success. He is filth. He is petty, whiny, murderous, indefensible, childish, and utterly painful. Of all the companions, he is the one Raistlin should have officially betrayed. Settling debts is wonderfully honourable -- especially when you are the supposed embodiment of evil -- but there are some debts that would be better left unpaid. Raistlin's to Tanis is one of those.<br /><br />Perhaps you are angry at me for badmouthing Tanis. Fair enough. But I chose everyone over him every time I read this story -- including Toede. Boo, Tanis! Just boo. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6323850202867966959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1613685419?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tokio Myers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tokio Myers" href="/user/show/28412182-tokio-myers">Tokio Myers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780786915897" href="/book/show/362787.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28412182-tokio-myers?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28412182-tokio-myers?shelf=ownedbooks">ownedbooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1613685419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1820333083002464996"><i>“The darkness might conquer, but it could never extinguish hope. And though one candle, or many, might flicker and die, new candles would be lit from the old. Thus hope’s flame always burns, lighting the darkness until the coming of day.”</i><br/><br/>The Dragonlance Chronicles comes to an end and man was it an adventure. Dragonlance isn't the best written or unique series out there in the vast ocean of fantasy, but it's one that makes you smile with predictable story lines and tropes that sometimes make your</span>
  <span id="freeText1820333083002464996" style="display:none"><i>“The darkness might conquer, but it could never extinguish hope. And though one candle, or many, might flicker and die, new candles would be lit from the old. Thus hope’s flame always burns, lighting the darkness until the coming of day.”</i><br /><br />The Dragonlance Chronicles comes to an end and man was it an adventure. Dragonlance isn't the best written or unique series out there in the vast ocean of fantasy, but it's one that makes you smile with predictable story lines and tropes that sometimes make your eyes role. That's what I like about this series, it pushes you into a world you know with characters you can't help but love (except for Laurana and Tika). It brings you to a world of dragons that are gods (totally badass) and evil mages. It has strong characters, weak ones, the ones that you should fear, and the tricksters. <br />I feel like am a kid again chasing dragons and saving the princess (well prince for me).<br /><br /><i>“The ones we love most are those we trust least.” </i><br /><br />Even though this isn't the end of the adventuring group, it's a satisfying end with some hope for the future and an soft sort of ending that leaves the story open but you're not that salivating for the next book. The writing was young adult if anything and expect the expected but I would HIGHLY recommend this series to children, young adult, new adults (whatever that is), the old, and the young at heart. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1820333083002464996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3202376142" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3202376142" />
    <a title="Jim C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c"><img alt="Jim C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340034171p2/10296231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3202376142?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim C" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c">Jim C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3202376142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13890697095256904545">This is the third book of a trilogy and this series must be read in order. This one picks up right where we left off in the second book. In this one, our group of companions are mourning their loss of one of their friends and things are rough. Tanis has been gone for several days while the rest of the group are hiding out as they are on the run.<br/><br/>I have read this trilogy several times and my rating here is basically based on the nostalgia factor. This was my introduction into the fantasy genre and</span>
  <span id="freeText13890697095256904545" style="display:none">This is the third book of a trilogy and this series must be read in order. This one picks up right where we left off in the second book. In this one, our group of companions are mourning their loss of one of their friends and things are rough. Tanis has been gone for several days while the rest of the group are hiding out as they are on the run.<br /><br />I have read this trilogy several times and my rating here is basically based on the nostalgia factor. This was my introduction into the fantasy genre and this trilogy led me to many worlds. I will admit that I do believe this isn't the best written fantasy book. In fact, this one might be the weakest of the trilogy as there are several plot holes. I know a common complaint of these books is that they feel like a role playing adventure and this one is the one that I feel that the most. With all that being said I don't care as I still consider this a tremendous read. I love the new places that we discover on the adventure. I still love the characters and I feel for them as they suffer more loss and their situation seems to worsen each day. To me, the highlight of this book is the theme of love. Whether it is familial love, romantic love, or love of people that become your adopted family. This theme resonates throughout the book.<br /><br />One question to ask oneself when rating a book is which factors more. Is it the quality or how it makes you feel? Yes the quality isn't the best in this book but this book gives all kinds of feels. Several times I could feel my eyes get misty. Compound that with the nostalgia factor and this book easily is a five star rating for me and I know that I will be rereading it once again in the near future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13890697095256904545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18713375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18713375" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18713375?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=to-my-kids">to-my-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18713375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14577333935340289207">Of the original Dragonlance trilogy, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68378.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning__Dragonlance_Chronicles___3_' title='Dragons of Spring Dawning (Dragonlance Chronicles, #3) by Margaret Weis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragons of Spring Dawning</a> is not my favourite. Even so, it contains some excellent moments while serving as both a pseudo ending to the War of the Lance and a fine introduction to the Legends series.<br/><br/>Perhaps it is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68378.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning__Dragonlance_Chronicles___3_' title='Dragons of Spring Dawning (Dragonlance Chronicles, #3) by Margaret Weis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragons of Spring Dawning</a>'s transitional position that makes it impossible for it to be the best of the three. There is a real sense in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68378.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning__Dragonlance_Chronicles___3_' title='Dragons of Spring Dawning (Dragonlance Chronicles, #3) by Margaret Weis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragons of Spring Dawning</a> that we are not speeding towards a resolution of the War but a shift in hostilities from</span>
  <span id="freeText14577333935340289207" style="display:none">Of the original Dragonlance trilogy, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68378.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning__Dragonlance_Chronicles___3_" title="Dragons of Spring Dawning (Dragonlance Chronicles, #3) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Spring Dawning</a> is not my favourite. Even so, it contains some excellent moments while serving as both a pseudo ending to the War of the Lance and a fine introduction to the Legends series.<br /><br />Perhaps it is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68378.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning__Dragonlance_Chronicles___3_" title="Dragons of Spring Dawning (Dragonlance Chronicles, #3) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Spring Dawning</a>'s transitional position that makes it impossible for it to be the best of the three. There is a real sense in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68378.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning__Dragonlance_Chronicles___3_" title="Dragons of Spring Dawning (Dragonlance Chronicles, #3) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Spring Dawning</a> that we are not speeding towards a resolution of the War but a shift in hostilities from the vast and impersonal to the internal and personal. Which means that while the book is necessary in the greater arc of the series, it must fail to live up to the promise of its predecessors because it cannot, by its very nature, deliver a fitting end to all the threads of the story. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68378.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning__Dragonlance_Chronicles___3_" title="Dragons of Spring Dawning (Dragonlance Chronicles, #3) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Spring Dawning</a> generates a feeling that Weis and Hickman reached a point where their huge cast of characters was too much to handle. Gilthanas and Silvara, Goldmoon and Riverwind, Alhana Starbreeze, Lord Ariakas, Astinus, Raistlin (although that is rectified by the Legend series), and even Fewmaster Toade get short shrift. Their stories could have been the basis for at least two more books in the series proper, which also would have allowed for a stronger telling of the stories that it does manage to tell.<br /><br />Of course, many of these missing stories have been told by others in future installments of the Dragonlance universe, but one can't help wondering how much better these stories would have been if they'd been contextualized within the War itself and told by the originators of the series.<br /><br />Regardless, the stories that Weis and Hickman do manage to tell in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68378.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning__Dragonlance_Chronicles___3_" title="Dragons of Spring Dawning (Dragonlance Chronicles, #3) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Spring Dawning</a> are well told.<br /><br />It was particularly nice to see Tanis Half-Elven through the eyes of my four year olds, whom I read the book to. I always hated Tanis. I found his whining insufferable; I always felt the "supposed" darkness of his soul was a bit of a joke; I thought his attack on Berem was too easily forgiven by his friends, and nothing in my latest oral reading of the book changed my mind on any of these points. But something did change for me, and I was finally able to see how Tanis' role as leader can gloss over his faults for an audience as easily as it seems to for his friends in the book. Tanis seems to have a genuine charisma. I don't get it personally, but now at least I recognize how it works.<br /><br />The entire series is worth reading multiple times, and this is an important step along the way, but if you're anything like me don't expect to love this episode in the Dragonlance story. It is far from the best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14577333935340289207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1963014300" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1963014300" />
    <a title="Oliviu Crâznic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5613774-oliviu-cr-znic"><img alt="Oliviu Crâznic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307829345p2/5613774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1963014300?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Oliviu Crâznic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Oliviu Crâznic" href="/user/show/5613774-oliviu-cr-znic">Oliviu Crâznic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5613774-oliviu-cr-znic?shelf=best-books-ever">best-books-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5613774-oliviu-cr-znic?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1963014300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3094769157128109129">„Foe after foe fell to Raistlin.”<br/><br/>Everything is falling apart for the Heroes of the Lance in this last volume.<br/>Sturm is dead and, unlike other characters of other stories, he stays dead; Flint is about to die and, unlike other characters of other stories, he is not to be saved; Kitiara is a betrayer and, unlike other characters in other stories, she stays a betrayer; and now Raistlin is willingly changing his red robe with a black one, leaving his brother and his friends to die a gruesome death by</span>
  <span id="freeText3094769157128109129" style="display:none">„Foe after foe fell to Raistlin.”<br /><br />Everything is falling apart for the Heroes of the Lance in this last volume.<br />Sturm is dead and, unlike other characters of other stories, he stays dead; Flint is about to die and, unlike other characters of other stories, he is not to be saved; Kitiara is a betrayer and, unlike other characters in other stories, she stays a betrayer; and now Raistlin is willingly changing his red robe with a black one, leaving his brother and his friends to die a gruesome death by the hands of the Dragon Highlord...<br />It was never a battle between Good and Evil, after all, the Heroes begin to accept: it is a battle between Kitiara, who wants the world for her Goddess of Darkness, and Raistlin, who wants the world for himself.<br />And yet there is out there a bumbling, mysterious old man with a great white beard, the only one who, strangely enough, scares Raistlin.<br />Some call him „Fizban the Fabulous”. Others call him „Paladine”.<br />He is, probably, God.<br /><br />NB The book is amazing. <br />The one star out is simply because I could not let the authors „unpunished” for staining such a flawless story with ONE feminist, highly unconvincing scene: Laurana is appointed Commander of Kinghts of Solamnia, and the little opposition she faces is due to the fact that... she is a woman; not because she is not human, not because she was never a member of that traditionalist Order; but because she is a woman.... <br />The authors could have reached the same goal just making her a „de facto” commander of Palanthas, which would have been quite natural: the Commander of the Knights and anyone else would have followed her for her dragonlance and for her brother`s „pet” dragons. <br />However, the authors favored policy over the natural course of the story.<br />Beyond this, the book is, as I said afore, absolutely amazing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3094769157128109129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2294912738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2294912738" />

Really enjoyed Fizban. <br/>Each (Raistlin, Tasselehoff, Tanis, Laurana) of them grow into different people by the end of the book, realizing and asserting their true identities.<br/>Of course there </span>

Really enjoyed Fizban. <br />Each (Raistlin, Tasselehoff, Tanis, Laurana) of them grow into different people by the end of the book, realizing and asserting their true identities.<br />Of course there is a sequel trilogy, Dragonlance Legends, which brings back some of these characters. <br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1329960276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1329960276" />
    <a title="Leona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34997235-leona"><img alt="Leona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438676712p2/34997235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1329960276?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leona" href="/user/show/34997235-leona">Leona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34997235-leona?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1329960276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer380913823405905688">This one took me longer to read and dragged more than the first two books but nonetheless it was an entertaining read. The whole series was a nice light reading break after all that serious grimdark.<br/><br/>The adventures are quite good and the companions splitting up and going on different adventures is fun to read. Kitiara is a compelling character, my personal hate for her notwithstanding. She is quite well written and not one-dimensional like most others. Fizban is my other favorite here and the sur</span>
  <span id="freeText380913823405905688" style="display:none">This one took me longer to read and dragged more than the first two books but nonetheless it was an entertaining read. The whole series was a nice light reading break after all that serious grimdark.<br /><br />The adventures are quite good and the companions splitting up and going on different adventures is fun to read. Kitiara is a compelling character, my personal hate for her notwithstanding. She is quite well written and not one-dimensional like most others. Fizban is my other favorite here and the surprise twist was well done too (even though I saw it coming from the earlier hints) and Laurana’s character growth was also well done. The love triangle between Tanis, Kitiara and Laurana was a bit more in your face and annoying in this book.<br /><br />The most shocking thing for me was the tragic deaths of two of the main characters, but then again Harry Potter gets a lot darker and many characters die.<br /><br />The humor is what makes this series cool. Things get dark and bad stuff happens, but the humor is always there. Most modern fantasy I read has little humor if any (with the exception of Mark Lawrence) and the light humor aspect is what makes Dragonlance Chronicles is a perfect summer read.<br /><br />I think Raistlin is the best character in the entire series. The world is more interesting than the characters except Raistlin and Fizban. All in all it’s a nice summer read and I think every fantasy geek, D&amp;D and role playing nerd needs to read it as part of the must-read essentials stack.<br /><br />I can’t wait to read the sequel series Dragonlance Legends and Raistlin Chronicles.<br /><br />Verdict: Read the whole series!<br /><br />This review can also be seen on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://leonahenry.wordpress.com/2015/08/05/book-review-dragons-of-spring-dawning-by-margaret-weis-and-tracy-hickman/">https://leonahenry.wordpress.com/2015...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="380913823405905688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_227352943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227352943" />
    <a title="Cheryl Landmark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4411217-cheryl-landmark"><img alt="Cheryl Landmark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514683615p2/4411217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227352943?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl Landmark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl Landmark" href="/user/show/4411217-cheryl-landmark">Cheryl Landmark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227352943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1549957494586502478">This was quite a satisfactory ending to the trilogy--although I suppose it's not really an ending since it appears to be a prelude to another series after this one. Nevertheless, the tale of the diverse group of companions fighting against the Dark Queen and her evil dragons was wrapped up relatively neatly, although I found the ending a bit rushed.<br/><br/>I didn't like Tanis quite as much in this book as I did in the first two. He seemed too full of anger and guilt and allowed the darkness in him to ov</span>
  <span id="freeText1549957494586502478" style="display:none">This was quite a satisfactory ending to the trilogy--although I suppose it's not really an ending since it appears to be a prelude to another series after this one. Nevertheless, the tale of the diverse group of companions fighting against the Dark Queen and her evil dragons was wrapped up relatively neatly, although I found the ending a bit rushed.<br /><br />I didn't like Tanis quite as much in this book as I did in the first two. He seemed too full of anger and guilt and allowed the darkness in him to overrule the good at times. I was quite impressed, however, by Laurana's character development, but when this happened, I was ready to reach into the book and shake some sense into her. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I couldn't believe how gullible and stupid she was to walk so readily and easily into Kitiara's trap! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Tas and Fizban remain two of my most favourite characters in this series. I felt sorry for poor Tas, whose cheerful and curious outlook on life was tested by tragedy and loss. And, as for Fizban, I knew all along there was something more to him than the muddle-headed wizard persona he presented to the world!<br /><br />Raistlin's obsessive bid for power turned him into a very creepy, cold character in this book, even more so than in the first two. It will be interesting to see what he does with his newfound powers in the next series.<br /><br />All in all, I enjoyed this fast-paced, classic epic fantasy and look forward to journeying with the companions once more on their subsequent adventures.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1549957494586502478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2569892301" />
    <a title="Allison ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55950436-allison"><img alt="Allison ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574092753p2/55950436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2569892301?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison ☾" href="/user/show/55950436-allison">Allison ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2569892301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1791753921879051647">
  <i>What if it does end in darkness, Tanis wondered for the first time. What will become of the world? What will become of those I'm leaving behind?<br/><br/>The darkness might conquer, but it could never extinguish hope. And though one candle, or many, might flicker and die, new candles would be lit from the old.<br/>Thus hope's flame always burns, lighting the darkness until the coming of day.</i>
<br/><br/><br/>The first 1/3 of this book was dragging on and on for me. The charm and clever wit was pushed to the side. I felt imp</span>
  <span id="freeText1791753921879051647" style="display:none">
  <i>What if it does end in darkness, Tanis wondered for the first time. What will become of the world? What will become of those I'm leaving behind?<br /><br />The darkness might conquer, but it could never extinguish hope. And though one candle, or many, might flicker and die, new candles would be lit from the old.<br />Thus hope's flame always burns, lighting the darkness until the coming of day.</i>
<br /><br /><br />The first 1/3 of this book was dragging on and on for me. The charm and clever wit was pushed to the side. I felt impatient and I just wanted to know what was going to happen. Eventually things do pick up, though much of the charm from the first two books is lost.<br /><br /><br />I noticed this series leaves large holes in the plot so people may want to go read other novels about the missing adventures. I probably won't do that anytime soon, but overall I am satisfied with the conclusion of this particular trilogy.<br /><br /><br />My biggest issue with this book was how the character development from the first two books seemed to flip flop back and forth. We would get some major character growth and then the character would do something totally out of the blue that just had me rolling my eyes. This is tough when it happens to THE MAIN CHARACTERS.<br /><br /><br />However, the plot of the story was pretty exciting. There were some plot twists I didn't see coming, and I would pick up this series again in the future to see what happens.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1791753921879051647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1176066326?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny" href="/user/show/7206839-jenny">Jenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780786915897" href="/book/show/362787.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7206839-jenny?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1176066326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16771471506183743869">This is a good conclusion to the companions' journey together. I didn't want it to end. My brother-in-law told me that many people love the world of Krynn, that it's a fantasy world many people feel attached to. I understand why. I would definitely read more books about Krynn, but I want them to be written by Weis and Hickman. They're not the best writers, but they make me connect to the characters. I love how the companions developed and changed from Dragons of Autumn Twilight to this book. The</span>
  <span id="freeText16771471506183743869" style="display:none">This is a good conclusion to the companions' journey together. I didn't want it to end. My brother-in-law told me that many people love the world of Krynn, that it's a fantasy world many people feel attached to. I understand why. I would definitely read more books about Krynn, but I want them to be written by Weis and Hickman. They're not the best writers, but they make me connect to the characters. I love how the companions developed and changed from Dragons of Autumn Twilight to this book. They each had a perfect ending, appropriate for who they are and what they went through. I love that the authors didn't shy away from allowing main characters to die. It makes the books more realistic. <br />I would definitely recommend this series to people who love fantasy. It's a worthwhile world to fall into, almost as compelling to me as Middle Earth, and in some ways, even more compelling because it feels more modern. I love high fantasy, but there's something nice about a little bawdy humor mixed in, sort of like The Last Unicorn, a little contemporary feel. <br />I'm happy with this ending. And I'm contemplating reading Dragons of Summer...something...even though it takes place many years after the ending of this book and isn't fully connected to it, from what I understand. We shall see if Krynn calls me back.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16771471506183743869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15893678966743864106">I started this series because some friends told me that they loved it more than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_' title='The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lord of the Rings</a>. That seemed like a fairly worth while recommendation.   <span id="freeText15893678966743864106" style="display:none">I started this series because some friends told me that they loved it more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_" title="The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a>. That seemed like a fairly worth while recommendation. I was certainly surprised to discover that this not even in the same league as Tolkien. They did say that it starts out a little rough, but once you get into it the story really takes off. Well, after finishing the book I kept wondering when it was going to get better. <br /><br />After finishing it I decided that I needed to re-examined all the recommendations that these people gave me. And completely ignored them. <br /><br />Comparisons to Tolkien aside, this is a badly written book. From a grammar position all the way to the overall narrative structure and character story arcs, this book (and the trilogy) is simply awful. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7219827360785521283">I really wanted to like this series. I really did. But the writing and the plot just can’t hold up to the standard that the great epic fantasies have. Maybe it’s a sign of when it was written, and maybe you had to read this at a certain age or certain time. But it just doesn’t hold up today. I would call this popcorn fantasy. If compared to the cinema world, this is a B-movie released direct to home video. There’s just something lacking in pretty much every aspect all around: The depth of the ch</span>
  <span id="freeText7219827360785521283" style="display:none">I really wanted to like this series. I really did. But the writing and the plot just can’t hold up to the standard that the great epic fantasies have. Maybe it’s a sign of when it was written, and maybe you had to read this at a certain age or certain time. But it just doesn’t hold up today. I would call this popcorn fantasy. If compared to the cinema world, this is a B-movie released direct to home video. There’s just something lacking in pretty much every aspect all around: The depth of the characters, the logic and believability of their decisions, the dialogue, the story, it’s pacing. I think that this is just going to appeal to nostalgic fans at this point.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2231667043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4318423667957523679"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/>I found that some parts of the story were a little long sometimes(more than with the two previous volumes). Satisfying and very intriguing conclusion for the trilogy. As we all know(right?) the world of Dragonlance(D&D in general) is complex and vast and it really seems like this <i>Chronicles</i> conclusion also serves as a prelude to the <i>Legends</i> trilogy. <br/><br/>So, not always a passionating read, might be a little dull sometimes, but not enough so I wouldn't pick up the book to continue my reading.</span>
  <span id="freeText4318423667957523679" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br />I found that some parts of the story were a little long sometimes(more than with the two previous volumes). Satisfying and very intriguing conclusion for the trilogy. As we all know(right?) the world of Dragonlance(D&amp;D in general) is complex and vast and it really seems like this <i>Chronicles</i> conclusion also serves as a prelude to the <i>Legends</i> trilogy. <br /><br />So, not always a passionating read, might be a little dull sometimes, but not enough so I wouldn't pick up the book to continue my reading. Overall it's still a very good book!</span>

        </div>

<div id="review_738782583" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/738782583" />
    <a title="Colin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/935022-colin"><img alt="Colin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203787624p2/935022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/738782583?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colin" href="/user/show/935022-colin">Colin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780786915897" href="/book/show/362787.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer17816907302660396165">Still enjoying re-reading this series. I'm not so into the Mormon subtext that pervades the Dragonlance books (not a slam against Mormonism itself, mind you, just seems weird in a fantasy series). Since I first read Dragonlance books back in the 80s, I always identified with Raistlin Majere. Not quite as much in my old age, but it's interesting to re-read and see why I loved the character so much . . . </span>

<div id="review_3530399893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3530399893" />
    <a title="Jackie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15308837-jackie"><img alt="Jackie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499192066p2/15308837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3530399893?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie" href="/user/show/15308837-jackie">Jackie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15308837-jackie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3530399893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17461394773323387254">Oh, boy. My thoughts on this book are so complicated. I finished it a week ago and it has taken me until now to sort them out and write this review. Initially, as I was listening this audiobook, I was enthralled. I was on the edge of my seat. It was amazing. I finished it and was satisfied. Initially.<br/><br/><br/>The more I think about it, the more I struggle with this initial impression with the book. This book, along with the series as a whole, has a lot of holes. You could argue a couple points here. Firs</span>
  <span id="freeText17461394773323387254" style="display:none">Oh, boy. My thoughts on this book are so complicated. I finished it a week ago and it has taken me until now to sort them out and write this review. Initially, as I was listening this audiobook, I was enthralled. I was on the edge of my seat. It was amazing. I finished it and was satisfied. Initially.<br /><br /><br />The more I think about it, the more I struggle with this initial impression with the book. This book, along with the series as a whole, has a lot of holes. You could argue a couple points here. First, I still haven't read Dragons of Summer Flame. I will, but not for a little while. That book is kind of a part of the Dragonlance Chronicles but is also a part of essentially the next generation. From my impression, this series was originally meant to be a trilogy. Meaning, this was supposed to be it. The end. The other argument is that there are numerous other series within the Dragonlance realm could fill this holes. <br /><br /><br />And I agree. But...<br /><br /><br />As this was initially meant to be a trilogy and this book wraps up the main conflict with a nice little bow, I really expect more out of a concluding book. Leave some endings open to be able to come back to the world? Yes. But this was more like, "I'm bored with this now, so I'm going to wrap it up and hopefully the readers won't notice all the things we don't address."<br /><br /><br />First off, lets talk about my favorite character Laurana. She had so much growth. She became a general. She was strong. And then she wasn't. She became a damsel in distress. She kind of redeems herself. I mean, she halfway gets herself out, but it still boils down to Tanis being there to save the day. This was a huge let down. I really thought she was bigger than that.<br /><br /><br />Speaking of Tanis, I actually liked him in this book. He had to make some really hard decisions and go against his morals. I like flawed heroes. I thought he was more relatable in this book than the previous two. Of all the characters, he had the most significant development, in my opinion. <br /><br /><br />Raistlin... Raistlin had significant development, too, but it is totally glazed over. What's worse is that his development plays a key role in the final altercation, but I have very little idea of how he got there. I get it. He is a mysterious character and has been since day one, but couldn't we get a little bit more about his transformation? I felt cheated.<br /><br /><br />Although, at least he had some transformation, unlike his brother, Caramon. You can take Caramon at the inn in Solace and put him side by side with Caramon outside of Neraka and they are exactly the same person. I actually felt bad for him because of this lack of development.<br /><br /><br />Kitiara was a bad guy that I wanted to like. She showed promise with her first appearance. But her character did not expand from that at all. She is manipulative and sleeps with everyone. That is it. I wasn't expecting her to be the bad guy turned good, and quite honestly, I didn't want her to be. But again, I was hoping for more depth from her. I thought Ariakas had more depth and he had a fraction of the page time that she did.<br /><br /><br />The other issue I had is how they just wrote off major supporting characters. I was totally expecting Alhana Starbreeze to make a comeback and address Sturm's death. Nope. Sturm is barely mentioned as well, come to think of it. Tika is basically thrown into the background as Caramon's arm candy. Goldmoon and Riverwind are just written off. Tanis and the gang literally waved goodbye and that was the end of them. I have no idea what happens to Elistan. Laurana mentions him once and that's it. The entire order of the Knights of Solamnia are just gone. Sturm is dead, so their role is done. Gilthanas and Silvara, you ask? Don't know that either! They showed up briefly at the Great Library and that's the last they are heard from. And then there was the blacksmith... What was his name again? He did forge the dragonlances, afterall. He should play some role in the finale.<br /><br /><br />How about the dragons... The good dragons? The evil dragons? This is a book about dragons after all. It's in the title. They're there... I think. This series is called Dragonlance, but from my reading/listening, the dragonlances themselves played little role in the outcome. The dragons themselves didn't play much of a part in the end either.<br /><br /><br />As I am writing this, I keep thinking of more and more plot points that are never revisited. The refugees of Pax Tharkas, the dwarves they take refuge with, the refugee elves. The longer I think, the more I come up with. However, I think I will let it rest.<br /><br /><br />There are so many plot elements and characters that are introduced simply to further the plot and then just forgotten about. It's like the authors were hoping that we weren't paying attention. Which is a shame, because the premise of the books had so much promise. <br /><br /><br />Initially, I rated this book four stars. It was by far my favorite of the three, and despite all of these misgivings I stand by it being my favorite. But upon further reflection, I am going to demote it down to two and half stars. I want so badly to keep it as a four star book, but with all of these holes, I can't. I will eventually go back to Krynn, and I hope these characters get the resolution that they were cheated, but as the end of an era with this band of heroes and the official end of a trilogy, it was not a solid ending. A lot was left to be desired.<br /><br /><br />As a series, I would recommend picking it up as an easy read, especially if you are just getting into fantasy for the first time. It's a good starter series for the genre, but does not compare with other writers such as J.R.R. Tolkien or Robert Jordan.<br /><br />Check out my other reviews on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://jaxsbooknook.blogspot.com">https://jaxsbooknook.blogspot.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17461394773323387254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3518604262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3518604262" />
    <a title="Tabitha " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5863594-tabitha"><img alt="Tabitha " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513129123p2/5863594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3518604262?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tabitha " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tabitha " href="/user/show/5863594-tabitha">Tabitha </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3518604262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13179421074087157637">This review is also featured on <a href='https://www.behindthepages.org/post/dragons-of-spring-dawning-by-margaret-weis-and-tracy-hickman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Behind the Pages: Dragons of Spring Dawning</a><br/><br/>Takhisis gathers her armies at Neraka, ready to march on the rest of Krynn and burn it to the ground. The companions armed with both Dragonlances and Dragons Orbs race to put an end to Takhisis’s armies. But along the way, they will have a hard road to follow. One that will divide them and cause them to make difficult choices. Can the companions survive what awaits them?<br/><br/>The companions must venture from one challenge to an</span>
  <span id="freeText13179421074087157637" style="display:none">This review is also featured on <a href="https://www.behindthepages.org/post/dragons-of-spring-dawning-by-margaret-weis-and-tracy-hickman" rel="nofollow noopener">Behind the Pages: Dragons of Spring Dawning</a><br /><br />Takhisis gathers her armies at Neraka, ready to march on the rest of Krynn and burn it to the ground. The companions armed with both Dragonlances and Dragons Orbs race to put an end to Takhisis’s armies. But along the way, they will have a hard road to follow. One that will divide them and cause them to make difficult choices. Can the companions survive what awaits them?<br /><br />The companions must venture from one challenge to another as they race to save Krynn and there is plenty of action to go around. Lingering questions from the first two books will be answered, and some of those answers may surprise readers. And as everything winds down every one of the companions will reach the end of their developmental arc, leaving them all as vastly different characters from when the reader first met them.<br /><br />Being the series it is, Dragonlance offers readers many opportunities to expand their knowledge of the races, history of Krynn and just about any character they encounter in The Chronicles. There are some gaps in the story that the reader has to fill themselves. A first-time reader may be confused, but trust me, the information is out there. Enough hints are dropped to form an idea of what happened within Dragons of Spring Dawning, but the full stories are contained in supplemental books. And they are definitely worth investing time into.<br /><br />I lingered on this book, trying to savor the adventures as long as I could. I was happy to say that I didn’t remember the ending exactly and it was great experiencing it all over again. And just like the first time I finished reading Dragons of Spring Dawning, I wanted to dive into the other books in the Dragonlance series to learn more. The companions will face their toughest challenges yet and will have to confront heartbreak and loss. Dragons of Spring Dawning is a powerful end to an engaging trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13179421074087157637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2161396343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2161396343" />
    <a title="Helen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15413983-helen"><img alt="Helen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481815064p2/15413983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2161396343?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen" href="/user/show/15413983-helen">Helen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140087208" href="/book/show/893839.Dragons_of_Spring_Dawning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=hated-the-main-character">hated-the-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=dragon">dragon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2161396343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14322533660561827622">What has happened to Tanis? Since the first book, he has lost all his confidence and his emotional intelligence has devolved to the level of a 12-year-old. He doesn't seem to care about his friends or stopping the dragon army. <br/><br/>Laurana has gone the other way, almost like the characters have swapped roles. She went from being a lovesick woman trailing after Tanis, to finding the dragonlances and then becoming the general of an army! I loved the way her character developed and it felt like the book</span>
  <span id="freeText14322533660561827622" style="display:none">What has happened to Tanis? Since the first book, he has lost all his confidence and his emotional intelligence has devolved to the level of a 12-year-old. He doesn't seem to care about his friends or stopping the dragon army. <br /><br />Laurana has gone the other way, almost like the characters have swapped roles. She went from being a lovesick woman trailing after Tanis, to finding the dragonlances and then becoming the general of an army! I loved the way her character developed and it felt like the book was going to be Laurana's story, but then she goes and does something very silly and drops out of the story almost completely, reappearing again only when required to be Tanis' love interest, to give him a reason to feel conflicted. A shameful waste of a brilliant character.<br /><br />I appreciate the authors trying to bring in a darker edge but I don't think it worked. Tanis was supposed to be fighting the darkness in himself, I think? But it just made him seem immature and whiny. Major characters were killed off to try to highlight how serious things were getting but their deaths didn't have much impact.<br /><br />The storylines felt messy and the big holes in them continued. Having to read another series of books to fill in the details that were left out of these books is just bizarre. Either write an epic, sprawling fantasy or write a neat and tidy one. Trying to do both like this doesn't work. I could read the other books (The Lost Chronicles?) but I know how they end so what really is the point? <br /><br />The stereotyping of characters was taken too far in this book. Red and green dragons are evil, bronze and silver dragons are good (and actually called 'the good dragons' in the book many times). All Minatours have bad tempers. Kenders are lighthearted and can't grasp other people's ideas of ownership. Elves are proud and arrogant. <br /><br />Characters were rarely allowed to step outside of their roles. It's lazy writing, and irritating because it supports the idea that people in different groups or cultures all have the same characteristics and behave in the same way.<br /><br />Dragons of Spring Dawning lost the fluffy, fun vibe that made the earlier books such fun to read. It felt lazily written and the messy storylines and overwhelming stereotyping and sexism made this a disappointing finish to the series. To be honest I'm a bit angry with it now. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14322533660561827622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_851456802" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/851456802" />
    <a title="Mike Rice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25075923-mike-rice"><img alt="Mike Rice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546657236p2/25075923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/851456802?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike Rice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike Rice" href="/user/show/25075923-mike-rice">Mike Rice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer851456802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer449289700112976871">Until recently, Dragonlance had been a whisper of my youth carried by me fondly into adulthood. A dear friend of mine, Christie Bilboa (of bilbosbookends.com) encouraged me to revisit the prolifically imaginative and colorful world of magic, wonder and danger as a group reading effort. Having 'remembered' reading this series before, but remembering only bits and pieces of it, I agreed. What I soon learned is that not only was Dragonlance a whisper of my past, but the whisper wasn't even mine. I </span>
  <span id="freeText449289700112976871" style="display:none">Until recently, Dragonlance had been a whisper of my youth carried by me fondly into adulthood. A dear friend of mine, Christie Bilboa (of bilbosbookends.com) encouraged me to revisit the prolifically imaginative and colorful world of magic, wonder and danger as a group reading effort. Having 'remembered' reading this series before, but remembering only bits and pieces of it, I agreed. What I soon learned is that not only was Dragonlance a whisper of my past, but the whisper wasn't even mine. I had, as it turns out, read only parts of the story (mostly from the Twins series) and had, apparently, filled in the blanks with the tales and recollections of friends and other fans. Normally this would be a terrible discovery, indicating a horrible lapse in memory, but as it turned out this was a added bonus that allowed me to (truly) 'rediscover' the world of Krynn all over again... and it was marvelous. <br /><br />This final installment in the Chronicles really was a fantastic work that brought the whole story together. The characters in this series are just so incredibly worth of personal investment and they drive the plot and tale along as hacks, slashes and adeptly negotiates it way through the darkness and evil of the Dark Queen Takhisis and her formidable army of servants: powerful dragons, power hungry Highlords and wretched and loathsome servants. Perhaps one of the incredibly formative aspects of the characters is the emotional evolution, achieved through the roller coaster of events,that takes place - truly bringing them into the realm of believable and cherished personas. <br /><br />Unlike many tales, the lines between 'good' and 'bad' character is hard to differentiate because both the heroes and the villains of this tale are so intentionally driven by emotion and desire that the lines between them is blurred. <br /><br />I could go on and on, but read the book.. It's worth the time. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="449289700112976871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nYjZVlZFf8RyIkI4LJwPnNRao3PGvnsZGmgzh/BtF0R0gCEnSMR/LiWSA8ljeyzuNPMJh4VNuWspmvFOwtUvbA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gqxDZYwYyXeU8RIuPYErhhlxCJU5dUKifUiEx5DQPWxrpLsUkpnJncNBU99yZgj0+diiYXqGgNBOukYOomgFRA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11598991399137922434">Fantasy novelist who, along with Tracy Hickman, was one of the original creators of the <i>Dragonlance</i> game world. I've written numerous novels and short stories set in the world of Krynn, as well as series in other, original worlds. These include: Darksword, Rose of the Prophet, Star of the Guardians, DeathGate, Dragonvarld, Sovereign Stone, Dragonships, and the Dragon Brigade. I also wrote two para</span>
  <span id="freeText11598991399137922434" style="display:none">Fantasy novelist who, along with Tracy Hickman, was one of the original creators of the <i>Dragonlance</i> game world. I've written numerous novels and short stories set in the world of Krynn, as well as series in other, original worlds. These include: Darksword, Rose of the Prophet, Star of the Guardians, DeathGate, Dragonvarld, Sovereign Stone, Dragonships, and the Dragon Brigade. I also wrote two paranormal romance novels, Fallen Angel and Warrior Angel, with my daughter, Elizabeth Baldwin. I graduated from the University of Missouri–Columbia and now live in Wisconsin with dogs, Max, Dixie, Joey the Thug and Clancy the Hooligan. <br /><br />I am currently working on the third book in the Dragon Brigade series, the Seventh Sigil. The first book is Shadow Raiders. The second book is Storm Riders, coming out from Tor in July 2013. <br /><br />My hobby is flyball racing with my dogs, Dixie, a border collie, and two crackhead Shelties, Joey the Thug and Clancy the Hooligan. <br /><br />I am the owner of the company, Margaret Weis Productions, publisher of RPGs. Our newest project is creating the RPG for the wonderful TV series, Firefly. Shiny!</span>
